CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in 15% taste bud cells in circumvallate
CC       and foliate papillae but only in 2% in fungiform papillae.
CC       Expressed in gastric and duodenal tissues.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RP   TISSUE SPECIFICITY.
RX   PubMed=16720576; DOI=10.1074/jbc.M513637200;
RA   Behrens M., Bartelt J., Reichling C., Winnig M., Kuhn C., Meyerhof W.;

RT   taste receptor expression.";
RL   J. Biol. Chem. 281:20650-20659(2006).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC       Expressed in testis (PubMed:16720576).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16720576}.
CC   -!- POLYMORPHISM: Variations in TAS2R38 are associated with the
CC       ability to taste phenylthiocarbamide (PTC tasting) [MIM:171200];
CC       also called thiourea tasting. The ability to taste the substance
CC       PTC and a number of related substances is genetically controlled.
CC       Genetic studies have demonstrated complex inheritance for this
CC       trait. For some people (and some chimpanzees also), the chemical
CC       PTC tastes very bitter. For others, it is tasteless. Actually,
CC       substantial variation in taste sensitivity exists in human. Five
CC       haplotypes arising from three coding SNPs in the TAS2R38 gene are
CC       associated with distinct phenotypes of PTC taste sensitivity.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       Activated by the sulfonyl amide sweeteners saccharin and
CC       acesulfame K. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.

CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.

CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity). In
CC       airway epithelial cells, binding of bitter compounds increases the
CC       intracellular calcium ion concentration and stimulates ciliary
CC       beat frequency (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}. Cell
CC       projection, cilium membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}. Note=In
CC       airway epithelial cells, localizes to motile cilia.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC       Expressed on ciliated airway epithelium.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and exclusively in gustducin-positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000305}; Multi-pass membrane
CC       protein {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in 15% taste bud cells in circumvallate
CC       and foliate papillae but only in 2% in fungiform papillae.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in 15% taste bud cells in circumvallate
CC       and foliate papillae but only in 2% in fungiform papillae.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in 15% taste bud cells in circumvallate
CC       and foliate papillae but only in 2% in fungiform papillae.
CC       Expressed in the duodenum, antrum and fundus (part of the
CC       stomach). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11854532}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: This protein was previously referred to as T2R26 or T2R12
CC       but is now considered to be the ortholog of human TAS2R41.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5.

CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in the antrum and fundus (part of the
CC       stomach), duodenum and in gastric endocrine cells.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11854532}.

CC       single taste receptor cell.

CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled cycloheximide receptor implicated in
CC       the perception of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the
CC       gastrointestinal tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-
CC       regulated cation channel TRPM5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10761935,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15759003}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in gastric and duodenal tissues.
CC   -!- POLYMORPHISM: Variations in Tas2r105 are associated with avoidance
CC       of cycloheximide at low concentrations.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10761935}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Mice fail to avoid cycloheximide at low
CC       concentrations and show a lack of cycloheximide-induced action
CC       potentials in a principal nerve innervating taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15759003}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12379855,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15759003}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with RTP3 and RTP4.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16720576}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16720576};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in a subset of gustducin-positive
CC       taste receptor cells of the tongue. Expressed in circumvallate
CC       papillae and testis (PubMed:16720576).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16720576}.
CC   -!- POLYMORPHISM: The Lys-172 polymorphism in TAS2R16 is associated
CC       with genetic susceptibility to alcoholism [MIM:103780].
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Confers bitter perception of salicin to non-taster
CC       mice.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5 (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in testis (PubMed:16720576).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16720576}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled strychnine receptor implicated in the
CC       perception of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the
CC       gastrointestinal tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-
CC       regulated cation channel TRPM5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15759003}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5.

CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor for denatonium and N(6)-
CC       propyl-2-thiouracil implicated in the perception of bitter
CC       compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal tract.
CC       Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation channel
CC       TRPM5. In airway epithelial cells, binding of denatonium increases
CC       the intracellular calcium ion concentration and stimulates ciliary
CC       beat frequency. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}. Cell
CC       projection, cilium membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}. Note=In
CC       airway epithelial cells, localizes to motile cilia.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed on airway ciliated epithelium.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19628819}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Gustducin-coupled receptor implicated in the perception
CC       of bitter compounds in the oral cavity and the gastrointestinal
CC       tract. Signals through PLCB2 and the calcium-regulated cation
CC       channel TRPM5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10761934,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10761935}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells. Expressed in the antrum and fundus (part of the
CC       stomach), duodenum and in gastric endocrine cells.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10761934}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Several bitter taste receptors are expressed in a
CC       single taste receptor cell.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor that may play a role in the perception of
CC       bitterness and is gustducin-linked. May play a role in sensing the
CC       chemical composition of the gastrointestinal content. The activity
CC       of this receptor may stimulate alpha gustducin, mediate PLC-beta-2
CC       activation and lead to the gating of TRPM5.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in subsets of taste receptor cells
CC       of the tongue and palate epithelium and exclusively in gustducin-
CC       positive cells.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Most taste cells may be activated by a limited
CC       number of bitter compounds; individual taste cells can
CC       discriminate among bitter stimuli.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor T2R family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
